  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a5f2113-4c0e-4e00-b7be-da310f9dd34e'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2635492689039968321">Three hundred years after the events of the Mistborn trilogy, Scadrial is now on the verge of modernity, with railroads to supplement the canals, electric lighting in the streets and the homes of the wealthy, and the first steel-framed skyscrapers racing for the clouds.<br/><br/>Kelsier, Vin, Elend, Sazed, Spook, and the rest are now part of history—or religion. Yet even as science </span>
  <span id="freeText2635492689039968321" style="display:none">Three hundred years after the events of the Mistborn trilogy, Scadrial is now on the verge of modernity, with railroads to supplement the canals, electric lighting in the streets and the homes of the wealthy, and the first steel-framed skyscrapers racing for the clouds.<br /><br />Kelsier, Vin, Elend, Sazed, Spook, and the rest are now part of history—or religion. Yet even as science and technology are reaching new heights, the old magics of Allomancy and Feruchemy continue to play a role in this reborn world. Out in the frontier lands known as the Roughs, they are crucial tools for the brave men and women attempting to establish order and justice.<br /><br />One such is Waxillium Ladrian, a rare Twinborn who can Push on metals with his Allomancy and use Feruchemy to become lighter or heavier at will. <br /><br />After twenty years in the Roughs, Wax has been forced by family tragedy to return to the metropolis of Elendel. Now he must reluctantly put away his guns and assume the duties and dignity incumbent upon the head of a noble house. Or so he thinks, until he learns the hard way that the mansions and elegant tree-lined streets of the city can be even more dangerous than the dusty plains of the Roughs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2635492689039968321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/47945427-aaron-okuyo-toponce"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1574373605i/47945427._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/47945427-aaron-okuyo-toponce">Aaron (Okuyo) Toponce</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I really liked this book. Fantastically so, actually. I was skeptical that a western could work as a fantasy, but Brandon nailed it, IMO. And "Shadows<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I really liked this book. Fantastically so, actually. I was skeptical that a western could work as a fantasy, but Brandon nailed it, IMO. And "Shadows of Self", the actual first book in the Wax and Wayne era, was a continuation to it, and absolutely fantastic.<br /><br />For me, the first three had a very Dark Ages feel, with deep political and philosophical undertones. It was "dark" and "heavy"; a very depressing read. Alloy of Law contrasts that, in that it is very "light" and "fun".<br /><br />IMO, it's better than the original trilogy, and Shadows of Self is even better.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_315662446" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/315662446" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/315662446?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315662446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8837233904000302208">As always, after reading something by Sanderson, I find myself irritated at how good he is. <br/><br/>So let's take it as a given that the book has all the essential ingredients: character, plot, dialogue, mystery, and action. All of these things are there, some of them merely great, most of them included to exceptional degree. <br/><br/>What truly impresses me though, is that Sanderson has done something extraordinarily unique with this book. Something that just isn't done in fantasy. <br/><br/>First, Sanderson wrote the Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText8837233904000302208" style="display:none">As always, after reading something by Sanderson, I find myself irritated at how good he is. <br /><br />So let's take it as a given that the book has all the essential ingredients: character, plot, dialogue, mystery, and action. All of these things are there, some of them merely great, most of them included to exceptional degree. <br /><br />What truly impresses me though, is that Sanderson has done something extraordinarily unique with this book. Something that just isn't done in fantasy. <br /><br />First, Sanderson wrote the Mistborn trilogy, an amazingly good fantasy trilogy set it in a unique, carefully-constructed world with a well defined magic system. <br /><br />Then he moved that world forward 300 years. He evolved it away from the low-industrial/dark-ages culture into a much more modern setting. <br /><br />This simply isn't done. <br /><br />You see, here's the way things work: <br /><br />1. You either write secondary world fantasy which is pretty medievally, or Renaissance-y, or occationally dark-ages-ish. Maybe you go crazy and make it kinda Asian. Or you make it bronze age. That's rare though. Pretty fringe. <br /><br />2. Your other option is to set something in THIS world. Most of the time when you do this, the setting is modern, which gets you urban fantasy. If you're not quite so modern, you get steampunk. If you go back further than that, it's alternate history. But again, that's kinda rare. <br /><br />These are the rules. They're not written down anywhere, but generally speaking, that's how things work. This is just the way things are done. <br /><br />But Sanderson has done something different here. Two somethings, actually. <br /><br />1. He evolved his world through time, changing the society significantly while staying true to the world he established in the earlier Mistborn books. <br /><br />(Yeah yeah. There have been a few other authors that have done this. Frank Herbert, for example. But it's so rare as to be practically unique. And in my opinion Sanderson has done it better than Herbert did for the simple fact that I want to read Sanderson's future books in this world, while I just couldn't make it through the second Dune sequel.)<br /><br />2. Sanderson has written urban fantasy THAT ISN'T SET IN THIS WORLD. Call it what you want, urban fantasy, qua-western, steampunk, whatever. That's what he did. <br /><br />I read this book and found myself thinking, "What? You can do that? How come nobody's done this before?"<br /><br />This is what happens with all truly clever innovation. Once someone does it, it seems obvious. It seems like anyone could do it. <br /><br />But everyone didn't do it. Sanderson did. That's a very special sort of clever. <br /><br />What's my point? <br /><br />My point is that this book is good, and you should give it a try. <br /><br />My other point is that this book does something different, and pulls it off very smoothly, so you should give it a try. <br /><br />My last point is that Sanderson has now been added to a very short list of authors. Specifically, the list authors whom I wish to kill so that I might eat their livers and thereby gain their power. <br /><br />So yeah. My hat's off to you, Brandon. Watch your back. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8837233904000302208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_148212913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148212913" />
    <a title="Chris McGrath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/247727-chris-mcgrath"><img alt="Chris McGrath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556372871p2/247727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148212913?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris McGrath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris McGrath" href="/user/show/247727-chris-mcgrath">Chris McGrath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/247727-chris-mcgrath?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/247727-chris-mcgrath?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/247727-chris-mcgrath?shelf=own-in-arc">own-in-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/247727-chris-mcgrath?shelf=own-in-hardcover">own-in-hardcover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148212913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13539492187489143070"><b>Brandon Sanderson commented on this review via reddit! See below.</b><br/><br/>This review originally appeared on <a href='http://gunnersbooks.tumblr.com/post/11960492158/the-alloy-of-law-by-brandon-sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>my book blog</a>.<br/><br/>The original Mistborn trilogy was a masterwork of fantasy, artfully combining a cool magic system, detailed and lush worldbuilding, and a plot and characters that were incredibly enthralling, weaving them together so perfectly that every piece depended completely on every other piece. <br/><br/>Sanderson has spoken and written about his goal for the world he created: three trilogies, spanning m</span>
  <span id="freeText13539492187489143070" style="display:none"><b>Brandon Sanderson commented on this review via reddit! See below.</b><br /><br />This review originally appeared on <a href="http://gunnersbooks.tumblr.com/post/11960492158/the-alloy-of-law-by-brandon-sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">my book blog</a>.<br /><br />The original Mistborn trilogy was a masterwork of fantasy, artfully combining a cool magic system, detailed and lush worldbuilding, and a plot and characters that were incredibly enthralling, weaving them together so perfectly that every piece depended completely on every other piece. <br /><br />Sanderson has spoken and written about his goal for the world he created: three trilogies, spanning many centuries on the same world. Sometime in the future we will see an "urban fantasy" trilogy and finally a "science fiction" trilogy, all based on the same magic system and, if The Alloy of Law is any indication, religions and mythologies derived directly from the first series.<br /><br />But the author decided to give us a treat in the meantime, something that initially started out as a short story but due to an epic writing style, even "short" turns out to mean 300+ pages. And so we have this novel, in a setting similar to the American Old West, with the most notable difference of gunslingers with magical powers. <br /><br />Overall, this is a very fun action/mystery novel for anyone looking for something unique or genre-bending. The tone is a bit lighter than Sanderson's other work, so while crime and death and moral questions abound, it is still not quite so dark and serious as it could have been. I am certainly glad, though, that these ethical issues were not left out, as they are one of my favorite aspects of his writing. There are some great twists and turns, exciting gunfights enhanced by abilities to push and pull metal, manipulate time, and heal quickly, to name a few. <br /><br />Because it's a short novel, however, there is a distinct lack of Sanderson's trademark world building; the reader is largely left to imagine a vague western setting. It's also not nearly the intricately planned masterpiece his other novels tend to be, so expectations should be set appropriately for a more straightforward novel where the author is simply having some fun in his fictional playground.<br /><br />Some have claimed that this book stands on its own, and that one needn't read the original trilogy in order to enjoy it. That may be so, but I suspect that anyone who does will have a distinct sense of being left a little bit out of the loop. Many of the original characters are referenced in passing as parts of various religions, and so without that prior knowledge of the world's history, such a reader would be at a disadvantage. There are also a couple of more important passages that cannot be fully appreciated without knowing those characters. For those of us who loved the first trilogy, they point to an exciting potential aspect of the future trilogies, and make me very excited for the next Mistborn book, whenever that may arrive. <br /><br />In the end, the last couple chapters are the most meaningful, both to the story and to the world itself, so I would recommend that this not be the book that introduces you to the Mistborn series, as the best parts of the climax and resolution would go right over your head, and the trilogy novels are each superior to this one. Those books are the main courses; The Alloy of Law is just a delicious snack meant to hold you over until the next big feast.<br /><br />--<br /><br />Mr. Sanderson's gracious comment:<br /><br /><i>This is a really solid review of the book, Gunner. Thank you. You basically captured what I feel is the spirit of the book. One of my primary worries with this is that readers will expect too much. It's meant to be fun and enjoyable, but the shorter length and smaller scope means that it's not going to have the depth of the original trilogy or of TWoK.<br /><br />I kind of look at this like I view some of the great sf television series out there. Many, like DS9, had beautiful, long-running arcs with enormous scope. But occasionally, they'd stop to do a stand-alone episode that was just meant to be fun. That's what Alloy of Law is.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13539492187489143070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1036890823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036890823" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036890823?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105829" href="/book/show/10803710-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=mystery-crime-and-thrillers">mystery-crime-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036890823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3027891738102376124">Sanderson is the most original fantasy writer of his generation. Not only has he written a complex and intricate trilogy (the original mistborn novels) but he has also somehow rebooted it with a time gap of three hundred years without losing any of the original edge. It’s kind of weird really. I don’t think many writers could have achieved this quite as well. Sanderson’s world is fully visualised and explained, the world building is phenomenal. And to retain this is a new semi-nineteenth century</span>
  <span id="freeText3027891738102376124" style="display:none">Sanderson is the most original fantasy writer of his generation. Not only has he written a complex and intricate trilogy (the original mistborn novels) but he has also somehow rebooted it with a time gap of three hundred years without losing any of the original edge. It’s kind of weird really. I don’t think many writers could have achieved this quite as well. Sanderson’s world is fully visualised and explained, the world building is phenomenal. And to retain this is a new semi-nineteenth century setting, years on, is great. <br><br>The novel’s protagonist is a retired law bringer. He’s also an alomancer, a user of metals. Wax has finally put away his revolvers and returned to the life of a gentleman; he has given up a life of excitement and justice seeking for a life of sophistication and socialising. He’s now getting married. It doesn’t sound very fun does it? It could never last; some people are born for adventure, and some books demand it. Wax is one of those people, and this is one of those books, so it’s not really surprising when he eventually tries to escape from the pedantic and joyless situation that is his life and goes to hunt down some criminals. <br><br><i>“Wayne: You wanna know why I really came to find you?<br><br>Waxilliam: Why?<br><br>Wayne: I thought of you happy in a comfy bed, resting and relaxing, spending the rest of your life sipping tea and reading papers while people bring you food and maids rub your toes and stuff.<br><br>Waxilliam: And?<br><br>Wayne: And I just couldn't leave you to a fate like that...I'm too good a friend to let a mate of mine die in such a terrible situation.<br><br>Waxilliam: Comfortable?<br><br>Wayne: No. Boring.” </i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458600159i/18506908._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luckily for him, and old friend turns up. He needs some help with a new case, help only Wax’s expertise can deduce. Another ex-law bringer has gone rogue, and is now committing the very things he once sought to prevent. Naturally, Wax’s interest is peeked ever so slightly. He reluctantly begins to piece the case together, and as time goes on he realises how deep this case is. It’s not something simple. This is Sanderson after all. Behind the case is a powerful crime syndicate, one that poses a huge amount of danger. The rogue law bringer is much more than he seems. <br><br>So it all goes down in the usual mistborn style, which means pieces of metal flying around, people flying around too and the bad guys getting it handed to them. Though there is more to it than that. Not only can Sanderson write excellent plots along with great action, but he can also write convincing characters with real morale dilemmas. The antagonist isn’t a bad man. In another time he would have been a hero. But in this one he is a terrorist. His convictions are morally right, but his methods are terrible. This made the whole thing very interesting, as the conflict between the two men was a battle of rights, and wrongs. <br><br>I have high hopes for the rest of this series. This one was as good as the original books, which, for me, was really quite surprising. I expected it to feel different, but it was all very much the same. It will be interesting to see how far Sanderson takes these characters, if he goes as far as he did before, then wax has a lot of development coming his way. After the terrible ending of the Reckoners series, I need to be reminded exactly why Brandon Sanderson is so awesome and this book did exactly that. I might just go on and read the next one straight away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3027891738102376124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer42572829479171186">1.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466987697' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Final Empire</a> ★★★★★<br/>2.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1502940449?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Well of Ascension</a> ★★★<br/>3.) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1537756588?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hero of Ages</a> ★★★★<br/>3.5) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553337767' rel='nofollow noopener'>Secret History</a> ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>

    <blockquote>"Huh [...] tea's poisoned."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Oh, I loved finally experiencing this next era of the mistborn world, especially in a city called Elendale (be still, my heart)! Yet, I was not expecting this book to start out with a very tragic murder plotline where the bodies are arranged in a very specific pose, and for the actual story to be taking place five years later where Wax is very much still</span>
  <span id="freeText42572829479171186" style="display:none">1.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466987697" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a> ★★★★★<br />2.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1502940449?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension</a> ★★★<br />3.) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1537756588?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages</a> ★★★★<br />3.5) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553337767" rel="nofollow noopener">Secret History</a> ★★★★★<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Huh [...] tea's poisoned."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Oh, I loved finally experiencing this next era of the mistborn world, especially in a city called Elendale (be still, my heart)! Yet, I was not expecting this book to start out with a very tragic murder plotline where the bodies are arranged in a very specific pose, and for the actual story to be taking place five years later where Wax is very much still grieving that night. And when the kidnappings start happening again, especially when these people being kidnapped are from mistborn family lines. <br /><br />I also really love how mistborns are no longer a thing in this new day and age! At most people can have one alomatic ability and one feruchemic ability (twinborns)! And our main characters have some really cool and fun powers with these two abilities: <br /><br /><b>➽ Wax –</b> pushes steel &amp; can grow heavier and lighter <br /><b>➽ Wayne –</b> Can alter time &amp; heals quickly (can also make great disguises, but unrelated to metals and powers!) <br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this first installment in a very beloved universe! And I can’t wait to continue on! Also, I will forever be the biggest fangirl of a certain brother who is destined to continue his brother’s work. Okay, brb, crying. <br /><br /><b>Content and Trigger Warnings:</b> murder, death, mention and threat of rape, kidnapping, gore, and violence.<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58213322-melissa-h" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa</a>! ❤</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer315981866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18148957395122798714">I mean...Sanderson is just amazing. He writes so well, his characters are SO well-drawn, you simply can't stop reading. There's a feeling of completeness in his plotting that makes you feel completely taken care of. The worldbuilding is stunning and vibrant and new...it's just, kind of ridiculous.<br/><br/>This is a followup in the world of Mistborn, but you DONT need to read the first three to understand what's going on (you should read them though, because it is icing on the cake as far as details.) Thi</span>
  <span id="freeText18148957395122798714" style="display:none">I mean...Sanderson is just amazing. He writes so well, his characters are SO well-drawn, you simply can't stop reading. There's a feeling of completeness in his plotting that makes you feel completely taken care of. The worldbuilding is stunning and vibrant and new...it's just, kind of ridiculous.<br /><br />This is a followup in the world of Mistborn, but you DONT need to read the first three to understand what's going on (you should read them though, because it is icing on the cake as far as details.) This is a world with an amazing magic system, but vaguely steampunk/industrial-era in ambience. I went in without really remembering the first three, but the opening is one of the best I've read in a very long time. You INSTANTLY are drawn into the story.<br /><br />So, if you like high fantasy, or a urban fantasy, or anything like that, pick this up.</span>

<div id="review_1763338163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763338163" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763338163?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765368546" href="/book/show/13538824-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763338163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7667389827039375265">I'll be honest, I was really skeptical to start the spin-off series at first as I think very highly of the original Mistborn trilogy and I'm quite sure the spin-off won't be able to top it in terms of quality and its epic story. It left me wondering will it be worth it to invest more of my time in this spinoff series? <br/><br/>Now, after reading The Alloy of Law, I can say it's true that it doesn't top the original trilogy in terms of quality and epic scope. However, is it worth it to invest your time in</span>
  <span id="freeText7667389827039375265" style="display:none">I'll be honest, I was really skeptical to start the spin-off series at first as I think very highly of the original Mistborn trilogy and I'm quite sure the spin-off won't be able to top it in terms of quality and its epic story. It left me wondering will it be worth it to invest more of my time in this spinoff series? <br /><br />Now, after reading The Alloy of Law, I can say it's true that it doesn't top the original trilogy in terms of quality and epic scope. However, is it worth it to invest your time in this series? yes, you're damn right it's worth it. It's worth every second of your time and fans of the original trilogy will almost definitely find this book very entertaining. Just remember that this time the story is much more light-hearted and suitable for everyone, don't come into this expecting something dark, grand and epic like the original trilogy.<br /><br />Instead of writing the book like the previous trilogy, Sanderson decided to give a new atmosphere to the settings of the world. Rather than the ash-fallen dark world from before, the setting is now more towards Steampunk and Western. The result is great to say the least, there are tidbits and quite a few nostalgia factors that you'll notice in its world-building and stories, even from the first page where it shows you the map and the name of the town, "Elendel". I can go on for thousand of words explaining about all the nostalgia factors but it would be better that I don't spoil it for you. Not to mention the characters are brilliantly well done, Wax &amp; Wayne is an endearing duo, they're super funny, interesting and reading their journey will definitely put a smile on your face.<br /><br />I definitely recommend this book to any Mistborn fans, just think of this as a chance to visit Scadrial after your adventure with Vin, Kelsier, Elend and the gangs. You'll find it worthwhile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7667389827039375265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1459734124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459734124" />
    <a title="Ikram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17065991-ikram"><img alt="Ikram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505599855p2/17065991.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1459734124?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ikram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ikram" href="/user/show/17065991-ikram">Ikram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105836" href="/book/show/12065807-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=crews">crews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=fictional-boyfriends">fictional-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17065991-ikram?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459734124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer972536916984665465"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500734493i/23379397.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b>Another day, another great Sanderson book. </b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Some mistakes, though, you can’t fix by being sorry. Can’t fix them, no matter what you do.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I haven't written a review in a while because life has just been crazy lately, but this book definitely deserves a proper review. <br/><br/>Let's start at the very beginning. Somehow, Brandon Sanderson was able to rip my heart out and burn it just with the freaking <b>prologue. </b> How is that even possible? The only other author who managed to do that was Colleen Hoover </span>
  <span id="freeText972536916984665465" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500734493i/23379397.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>Another day, another great Sanderson book. </b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Some mistakes, though, you can’t fix by being sorry. Can’t fix them, no matter what you do.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I haven't written a review in a while because life has just been crazy lately, but this book definitely deserves a proper review. <br><br>Let's start at the very beginning. Somehow, Brandon Sanderson was able to rip my heart out and burn it just with the freaking <b>prologue. </b> How is that even possible? The only other author who managed to do that was Colleen Hoover with Confess, but that's another story. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lessie's death had a huge impact on Wax.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>His confidence took a serious blow and the guilt completely drowned him. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450894091ra/17482035.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>So Wax decides to go back to his house in the city of <b>Elendel</b> *cough* Mistborn references *cough* but of course, trouble follows him everywhere. <br><br><b>The magic System</b><br>I loved how we got to see more aspects of the magic system. So Mistborns are not a thing anymore, apparently. The best thing you can hope for is to be a Twinborn. At first I thought that would be too limiting and I was disappointed that the main character wasn't Mistborn but man oh man, was I wrong. There's SO much you can do with Allomancy and Feruchemy working together. I mean, Miles anyone? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500460275ra/23342458.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What's with all the Ian gifs? Just Ignore my obsession. Moving on. <br><br><b>The Dialogue </b><br>The relationship between Wax and Wayne gives me life. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Nothing else dangerous we could find. Other than Wayne’s body odor.” <br>“That’s the smell of incredibleness,” Wayne called from inside.” </blockquote>
</i><br>The dialogue in this book is just priceless. It's funny and witty and I can never get sick of it. <br><br><b>The Trillaume Situation</b><br>I could not pronounce this name for the life of me. I probably even spelled it wrong but I'm too lazy to go check. I'm sure you know who I'm talking about. The bloody butler. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So here's the thing, in Sanderson's books there's always this fake good guy. Somebody who ends up betraying us from the inner circle so I was keeping an eye out for that and I guessed it pretty early on that the freaking butler was gonna screw us at some point haha. Bonus points for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The Romance Situation</b><br>Okay, confession time. I kinda sorta like Lady Steris *collective gasp* I feel like in a weird way, I ... relate to her somehow? I mean she's definitely the stiffest person on earth but you gotta give it to her, the girl is organized and she knows her shit. There's something Hermiony about her and I like that.<br><br>I have nothing against Masari/ Marasi (still too lazy to go check). She's a kickass female character and you can't go wrong with that. I have a feeling she's going to be end game but we'll see. <br><br>Overall, this was such an enjoyable read. I read it in a 24 hour readathon and I feel like it made the experience even better for me. <br><br>I can't wait to jump into the rest of the series. <br><br>Thanks for reading, please share your thoughts.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3065493868?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105836" href="/book/show/12065807-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3065493868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4143254974287369901"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Once one becomes a man, he can and must make his own decisions. But I do offer warning. Even a good thing can become destructive if taken to excess.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>The Final Empire ★★★★ 1/2<br/>The Well of Ascension ★★★★★<br/>The Hero of Ages ★★★★ 1/4<br/>The Alloy of Law ★★★★ 1/4<br/><br/>🌟 I loved the first Mistborn trilogy very much and it is a series that I think about a lot, I think it made me realize that I prefer fantasy books with a hard magic system because it feels very smart to me! I was hesitant to jump into t</span>
  <span id="freeText4143254974287369901" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Once one becomes a man, he can and must make his own decisions. But I do offer warning. Even a good thing can become destructive if taken to excess.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The Final Empire ★★★★ 1/2<br />The Well of Ascension ★★★★★<br />The Hero of Ages ★★★★ 1/4<br />The Alloy of Law ★★★★ 1/4<br /><br />🌟 I loved the first Mistborn trilogy very much and it is a series that I think about a lot, I think it made me realize that I prefer fantasy books with a hard magic system because it feels very smart to me! I was hesitant to jump into the second Mistborn series because I don’t like Western settings and because the expectations would not make me enjoy it as much as I want.<br /><br />🌟 As soon as I started reading it, I realized that I was wrong and that I got into the story super fast, Wax and Wayne became real people in my mind very fast and I enjoyed their relationship very much! The dynamic between them as a grumpy serious guy and a goofy laid-back friend is not a new thing but it was very well written, specially that Wayne is much smarter than he appears to be!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“That hat looks ridiculous.”<br />“Fortunately, I can change hats,” Wayne said, “while you, sir, are stuck with that face.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />🌟 The plot is not as complicated as the first trilogy and is much more light-hearted! That being said, the book is still atmospheric and I love that, I did not expect to love the plot very much but I did and that is all thanks to the magic system. I did not think the magic system could get any better than in the original series but Sanderson outdid himself and could improve the system without destroying the legacy he built in the first trilogy. I am a big fan of the different kinds of magic systems in the book and just seeing how they work hand in hand together to bring something more awesome is mind-blowing. Nothing makes me happy as much as a smart book can do and I assure you that this was a very smart book!<br /><br />🌟 Summary: I think the expectations decide how much these books are enjoyable, I knew it was different than the original trilogy, in terms of plot and atmosphere and characters and that meant I went with different things in mind and these were exceeded, the book is fast-paced, very smart with amazing world-building and real characters, I can’t wait to see what the rest of the series has for me!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“To be of use in even a single burst of flame and sound is worth more than a lifetime of achieving nothing.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />A BR with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/65321843-azrah" rel="nofollow noopener">my favorite South African Reviewer :3</a></span>

<div id="review_2159791255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159791255" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159791255?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575105805" href="/book/show/11263063-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=adult-fantasy-sci-fi">adult-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159791255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10052509101265941663"><b>6/11/17 </b><br/><br/>I buddy read this with <b>Warda</b>, who shares my love and adoration for Mistborn & BS. <br/><br/>SO GOOD to be back into this world again. And as a huge fan of the Mistborn trilogy, I knew going in that this would in no way match the original series in terms of… well, epic-ness (for lack of better terms) however, I was still certain that it’d not disappoint. It is, after all, Mistborn #2! It was yet another damn fine work by the one and only.<br/><br/>If you're a fan of the original trilogy, you will undoubtedly</span>
  <span id="freeText10052509101265941663" style="display:none"><b>6/11/17 </b><br /><br />I buddy read this with <b>Warda</b>, who shares my love and adoration for Mistborn &amp; BS. <br /><br />SO GOOD to be back into this world again. And as a huge fan of the Mistborn trilogy, I knew going in that this would in no way match the original series in terms of… well, epic-ness (for lack of better terms) however, I was still certain that it’d not disappoint. It is, after all, Mistborn #2! It was yet another damn fine work by the one and only.<br /><br />If you're a fan of the original trilogy, you will undoubtedly enjoy this. TAoL is set about 300 years after The Hero of Ages and though it’s a series that stands on its own, to get the most out of it and a better understanding of the world, I highly recommend reading them chronologically starting with The Final Empire. <br />And while keeping this short and concise, here’s a little preview of what’s in store...<br /> <br />-- A new and exciting world that is more evolved and modernized with technology and cultural advancements. It is descriptive and logical where the characters we've come to know and love from the first series have become mythical legends and heroes. Oh, the feels.😞<br /><br />-- A refreshing blend of familiar and new magic system (which I won’t lie, I was confused by at first) however, Sanderson once again proves that he is the master of unique and badass magic systems. It's almost like he’s been blessed by the gods of Magical Systems (and that goes for all his books).<br /><br />-- Lovable and complex characters plus an awesome bromance (you know I'm a sucker for bromance). Wax and Wayne are the perfect pair and foils. Their relationship is built on a long-standing trust and faithfulness to one another and as opposites as they are, they perfectly compliment each other through and through. <br /><br />Wax is the staple of all Sanderson’s characters. He's the good, heroic and supposedly tormented LC while Wayne is the funny but always lovable sidekick who's never short of witty or snarky comebacks. <br />The side characters were also nothing short of awesomeness, from the intelligent and tough female lead to the misguided main antagonist. <br /><br />-- The action scenes are filled with great and wonderful imagery, full of Allomantic battles that’d translate beautifully to the movie screen. (I’m still waiting for a BS movie!)<br /><br />And last but certainly not least, the epilogue… *SIGH* he really is the king of epilogues.<br /><br /><br /><b>4/11/17</b><br /><br />Finally, finally, finally, back in the world of Mistborn!!! 😍</span>
  <a data-text-id="10052509101265941663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10883791776053510139"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Wayne, you can't make bets with people when they aren't there."</i>
</b><br/><br/>HOLD ON. <b>HOLD ON A SECOND.</b><b>
  <i>I NEED TO SAVOR HOW HAPPY I AM IN THIS MOMENT.</i>
</b><br/><br/>You guys, I cannot express how much I adore the <i>Mistborn</i> novels. The series is written so well, with characters that I love. <br/><br/>This was such a clever and seamless transition into a new <i>Mistborn</i> era. As we have seen, adding to an already golden series doesn't always work out for the best.<b>
  <i>I'm looking at you J.K. Rowling.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Wax and Wa</span>
  <span id="freeText10883791776053510139" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating: 4.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Wayne, you can't make bets with people when they aren't there."</i>

As we have seen, adding to an already golden series doesn't always work out for the best.<b>

The new setting with a western spin is <u>so refreshing!</u>This book was a great introductory piece, and I'm so excited to continue on with their story. Also special shout out to all those throwbacks to the original <i>Mistborn</i> trilogy, for they made my heart glad.<br /><br />Buddy read this one with my girls <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a> AND <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22200230-nafeeza" rel="nofollow noopener">Nafeeza</a>!!!</span>

<div id="review_2936736710" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936736710" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2936736710?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105829" href="/book/show/10803710-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✨ A ✨  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=cross-post">cross-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy">faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936736710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer955226337484262358"><u>Reasons to read Mistborn Era 2:</u><br/><br/><b>A. Wax and Wayne <br/>B. Wayne and Wax<br/>C. answers A and B</b><br/><br/><br/>Centuries have passed since the events of The Hero of Ages, our original friends are long gone, but their legacy remains. <br/><br/>Waxillium Ladrian has been a lawman in the Roughs, the wild lands outside the city where there is no law or justice, for twenty years. A tragic accident that kills his uncle and sister leaves him as the high lord of his house and Wax finds that he has to return to Elendel, the home of his childh</span>
  <span id="freeText955226337484262358" style="display:none"><u>Reasons to read Mistborn Era 2:</u><br><br><b>A. Wax and Wayne <br>B. Wayne and Wax<br>C. answers A and B</b><br><br><br>Centuries have passed since the events of The Hero of Ages, our original friends are long gone, but their legacy remains. <br><br>Waxillium Ladrian has been a lawman in the Roughs, the wild lands outside the city where there is no law or justice, for twenty years. A tragic accident that kills his uncle and sister leaves him as the high lord of his house and Wax finds that he has to return to Elendel, the home of his childhood. <br><br>At first Wax finds it difficult to put away his gun and take up the duties of being a high Lord responsible for thousands of employees and saving his House from destitution. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1582117697ra/28987339.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wax soon realises that the City is just as dangerous as the Roughs and he might need those guns back. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Funny, how quickly someone can stop calling you a miscreant and a rogue when they want your help”</b>
</i><br><br><br>I could wax poetic (see what I did there 👀) about Sanderson's writing but I think you all already know by now how much I love his easy style. People who hate being thrown into a story with little to no explanation will like Sanderson's way of explaining things without it being boring or repetitive.<br><br>It was so crazy reading all the familiar names from Era 1 that appear here all the time. It makes me so happy to see things related to Vin, Elend, Kelsier Sazed and Spook mentioned in their everyday language. The nostalgia was such a pleasant to the book<br><br>What also blew my mind was how advanced the people of Scadrial managed to new world that Harmony made for them at the end of Hero of Ages. <br><br>You can definitely see how much more developed they are compared to Era 1. Their buildings are taller. Cars, trains and electricity is bring introduced. <br><br>The most awesome for me was the use of guns (which we didn't get in the first trilogy) and how allomancers manipulate the metal. <br><br>And the allomancy?!! AMAZING. I shall not elaborate if you have still to read this book but <i>WOW</i>. I thought I knew how it all worked but Sanderson has introduced some new metals and abilities that just left me speechless. <br><br>I really loved the plot. The setting gave this book a very different feel. It was like reading a detective mystery that was part steam punk, part western but with metal magic. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1582117697ra/28987340.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With everything I've mentioned above what really made this book (and what I'm sure is going to make the rest of the books in this series) perfection, were the characters. Wax, Wayne and Marasi were such fun to read about. Wax and Wayne, especially, had some of the best banter I've ever read. <br><br><blockquote>“Wayne's a little attached to that hat," Waxillium said. "He thinks it's lucky."<br><br>Wayne: "It is lucky. I ain't never died while wearing that hat." <br><br>Marasi frowned. "I ... I'm not sure I know how to respond."<br><br>Wax: "That's a common reaction to Wayne.”</blockquote> <br><br><br>So far, everytime I finish a Sanderson book I am filled with happiness, awe and excitement to move on to the next one. I hope that feeling never goes away.<br><br>If you're still deciding whether to continue the Mistborn series after the original trilogy. Keep in mind that it is very different from Era 1 but it has its own brilliance. Please give this book a go, you won't regret it. <br><br><br>I had fun reading this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/54464244-hamad" rel="nofollow noopener">my fellow Wayne enthusiast</a><br><br><b>‹ 4.5 stars ›</b><br>___<br><b>My reviews for:</b><br><br><i>Era One</i><br><br>0.5 (short story): <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608045644" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eleventh Metal</a><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604499760" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606309355" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605049392" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages</a><br><br>Book 3.5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737859" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a><br><br><br><i>Era Two</i><br><br>Book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737014" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self</a><br>Book 6: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737748" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bands of Mourning</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="955226337484262358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_993848349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/993848349" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/993848349?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105829" href="/book/show/10803710-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=cosmere">cosmere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993848349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10025276292496944620">This isn’t Mistborn.<br/><br/>This is a fantasy retelling of <i>The Lone Ranger</i> meets <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>. With guns and gangsters. And magic.<br/><br/>Lord Waxillium Ladrian returns from his life as a lawman in the rural Roughs. Coming back to Elendel to assume the mantle of head of his house after his uncle’s untimely death, he engages in the social life of the urban nobility. Until Wayne appears, and all changes…<br/><br/><i>”I think it's one of his personal failings. I try to help him out by being damn near perfect, but so f</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10025276292496944620" style="display:none">This isn’t Mistborn.<br /><br />This is a fantasy retelling of <i>The Lone Ranger</i> meets <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>. With guns and gangsters. And magic.<br /><br />Lord Waxillium Ladrian returns from his life as a lawman in the rural Roughs. Coming back to Elendel to assume the mantle of head of his house after his uncle’s untimely death, he engages in the social life of the urban nobility. Until Wayne appears, and all changes…<br /><br /><i>”I think it's one of his personal failings. I try to help him out by being damn near perfect, but so far, that hasn't been enough.”</i><br /><br />The duo of Wax and Wayne is definitely one of the best sets of characters Brandon Sanderson has created. Wax is the refined gentleman who does everything with style. Wayne is the funny sidekick who is so much more than a funny sidekick. Together, they are legendary heroes from a world the people of the city know nothing about.<br /><br />The prologue of this book was absodamnlutely great. It was very… not Sanderson. Not that Sanderson with his normal repertoire is not good, but this was very different. And it remained that way throughout the book.<br /><br />Unfortunately, it got too simple by the end. This was to me a book that started out on top, and from there it could only go one way. The second half was nowhere near as good as the first, and neither the villain(s), the revelations nor the actual progress of the story were particularly complex in any way. The conclusion was slightly disappointing, but only based on the high standard set in the early parts.<br /><br />However (a rather big however), the epilogue gracefully saved the book. There were no less than two character appearances that I was waiting for (I think both were actually supposed to be surprising), and I absolutely loved when they finally showed up.<br /><br />There are three very interesting things to note. The first is that this is Mistborn for adults. Again, not that the first trilogy was a set of children’s books. But this book is not only considerably more violent, but also has a few subtle references to sex. It’s almost enough to make you forget that this is written by Brandon Sanderson. But then the wondrously simplistic writing sets in again and makes you remember.<br /><br />The second thing is of course the setting. Mistborn was never actually medieval fantasy, but the progress into an industrialised society with trains and cars and gunslingers is a good one. I would have liked even more focus on the technological, political and social development, but hey, we have three more books to go.<br /><br />The last thing is the only slightly negative one. If you know me and my fantasy tastes, you’ll know that I am deeply obsessed with nostalgia. Nothing is better when it comes to fictional literature for me. And Sanderson gives himself this brilliant opportunity to play on the feeling. He uses it… but nowhere near enough. There are a few place names (Elendel etc.) and mentions of the religions like the Church of the Survivor, but I would have liked to see much, much more. It might be that Sanderson was afraid to overdo it, which is understandable, but to me it was rather underwhelming. It might also be that he wanted to separate this world from the world of the first Mistborn trilogy, and that definitely works, for better or worse. The lack of nostalgia did not decrease the quality of the book or my enjoyment of it in any way, though; I’m just saying it could have been even better.<br /><br />In any case, I take what I can get. Like this…<br /><br /><i>”The Church of the Survivor taught that the mists belonged to him, Kelsier, Lord of the Mists. He appeared on nights when the mist was thick and gave his blessing to the independent. Whether they be theives, scholars, anarchists, or a farmer who lived on his own land. Anyone who survived on their own-or who thought for himself-was someone who followed the Survivor, whether he knew it or not.”</i><br /><br />All in all, this is a great addition to the Mistborn universe and the Cosmere as a whole. I must admit I thought early on that it would be a strong five-star and my favourite Sanderson book since <i>The Final Empire</i>. It unfortunately seems that it was not, but it still was incredibly enjoyable.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10025276292496944620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1904927189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904927189" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904927189?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11783190-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904927189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4041929830596975232"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br/><br/>What do you get when you combine one of the most prolific fantasy authors of our time with an old school Spaghetti Western? This book right here. With Alloy of Law, Sanderson built on the amazing world he created in the original Mistborn trilogy and gave us more of the fantastic system, but in a new era with new technology advances and the problems that come with progress. We see how the religion of that land grew and changed based on the events of the first trilogy, and h</span>
  <span id="freeText4041929830596975232" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br /><br />What do you get when you combine one of the most prolific fantasy authors of our time with an old school Spaghetti Western? This book right here. With Alloy of Law, Sanderson built on the amazing world he created in the original Mistborn trilogy and gave us more of the fantastic system, but in a new era with new technology advances and the problems that come with progress. We see how the religion of that land grew and changed based on the events of the first trilogy, and how the shape of the world has changed. <br /><br />I was hesitant the first time I read this book, and didn’t give it the chance it deserved. I thought the book was fun, but decided not to continue on to the second and third books. In hindsight, I really can’t recall why on earth I didn’t want more Wax and Wayne. Because <i>Rust and Ruin</i>, those two are a joy to read. They are the Batman and Robin of an otherworldly Wild West, but with more sassy banter and less moody brooding. Not that each man doesn’t have problems and demons from their respective pasts, because they most definitely do. They have their crosses to bear, but they can laugh anyway, because who doesn’t have some weight on their shoulders? <br /><br />Alloy of Law is mainly the story of Waxillium Ladrian, a noble who makes his mark as a lawman in the Roughs before returning to the city of Elendel. Wax is a powerful Twinborn, and an impressive marksman. He’s a dangerous man, but most definitely still a nobleman at his core. He’s our hero, and I really like him. I also appreciated the fact that our main character was in his forties instead of his teens or twenties. The maturity was a welcome change. He’s well fleshed out, and has plenty of personality. But my favorite character was Wayne. He’s also a Twinborn, and a master of disguise to boot. Every time he made an appearance, I immediately smiled. My favorite dialogue was always spoken by Wayne. The man is just so darn funny. <br /><br />There were other characters that I enjoyed too, that I hope to see more of in the next books. While I know from friends that Steris becomes a more central character in following books, I didn’t see enough of her to form much of an opinion. I did find her refreshingly blunt and endearingly awkward, and can’t wait to see her grow. My favorite female in this particular book was Marasi. She was sweet and smart and inquisitive and funny, and had more of a backbone than I expected. I just really enjoyed her.<br /><br />I wavered between four and five stars for this book, and settled on four after much internal debate. The reasons are very subjective, and have no bearing the quality of the book. There were two main writing decisions that kept my rating from being higher. First, the allomantic idioms kind of threw me out of the story whenever I came across them, though I appreciated what Sanderson was trying to do with them. An example would be “take it with a pinch of copper” instead of with a pinch of salt. There were a lot of these variations. And like I said, I <i>get</i> it, I really do. They’re cute, and they give some realism, because every society develops their own idioms after a while. They just disrupted the flow for me. Second, I’m just not the biggest fan of steampunk and flintlock. Which is totally not Sanderson’s fault, I just bogged down in the details of weapons and other technology. <br /><br />But that being said, I had a lot of fun reading this book, and I read more of Wax and Wayne’s adventures!<br /><br />For more of reviews, as well as my own fiction and thoughts on life, check out my blog, <a>Celestial Musings</a><br /><br />A buddy read with my loves, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22200230-nafeeza" rel="nofollow noopener">Nafeeza</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4041929830596975232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137853340?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105836" href="/book/show/12065807-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137853340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8743306489540813391">I mean, are we in any doubt that Sanderson is THE main man, THE author of epic and original fantasy?!<br/><br/>I swear, he's close to being a god. I cannot fathom how he writes books like this. Where does he get his ideas?<br/><br/>This glorious story is set 300 years after the events of The Hero of Ages. The transition to this world was just smooth and epic, with some of the lands and Houses being named after the characters in the Mistborn Trilogy. Safe to say I squealed numerous times and felt the need to cry as </span>
  <span id="freeText8743306489540813391" style="display:none">I mean, are we in any doubt that Sanderson is THE main man, THE author of epic and original fantasy?!<br /><br />I swear, he's close to being a god. I cannot fathom how he writes books like this. Where does he get his ideas?<br /><br />This glorious story is set 300 years after the events of The Hero of Ages. The transition to this world was just smooth and epic, with some of the lands and Houses being named after the characters in the Mistborn Trilogy. Safe to say I squealed numerous times and felt the need to cry as well.<br /><br />It follows probably one of the best duo, Wax and Wayne, who I became <b>obsessed</b> with. The wittiness, the constant banter even when everything was going to shits brought me pure and utter joy.<br /><br />This book is way more lighthearted than the original trilogy. It's different, in the best possible way, but still there's that thread that links it to that other world. I was endlessly reminiscing. Nani, who I was buddy reading with, and I couldn't stop geeking out! :D<br /><br />As for the plot, I feel we've probably only managed to scratch the surface with The Alloy of Law, to the point where I don't feel the need to mention it here in my review. It seems minute (and the story is mainly centred around those Wax and Wayne) and more than likely, there's a LOT more left to explore.<br /><br />P.S. THAT EPILOGUE FUCK ME! I NEED ANSWERS!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8743306489540813391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1963462117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963462117" />
    <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud"><img alt="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517124730p2/14717996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963462117?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>
