<div id="review_952043513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952043513" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952043513?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=adorable-alphas">adorable-alphas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952043513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9310615177112258609">Re-read before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16065004.Shadows_of_Self__Mistborn___5_' title='Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) by Brandon Sanderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadows of Self</a> is release with some Sanderson buffs in the <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/142441-sanctum-of-fantasy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sanctum of Fantasy</a>
</b><br/><br/>I'd forgotten so much. Wax, Wayne and Marasi together are hilarious. Definitely more light hearted than the first trilogy in the Mistborn world. I even think I found a few clues I missed the first time. Now I'm totally ready for the Shadows of Self release Oct 6<br/><br/><b>Original Review Jun 2014</b><br/><br/><b>4.5 Harmonic Stars</b> The Brandon Sanderson Buddy Read and Epic Adventure continues with <a>Athena</a> and <a>Alexa</a>. I had so much</span>
  <span id="freeText9310615177112258609" style="display:none">Re-read before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16065004.Shadows_of_Self__Mistborn___5_" title="Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self</a> is release with some Sanderson buffs in the <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/142441-sanctum-of-fantasy" rel="nofollow noopener">Sanctum of Fantasy</a>
</b><br><br>I'd forgotten so much. Wax, Wayne and Marasi together are hilarious. Definitely more light hearted than the first trilogy in the Mistborn world. I even think I found a few clues I missed the first time. Now I'm totally ready for the Shadows of Self release Oct 6<br><br><b>Original Review Jun 2014</b><br><br><b>4.5 Harmonic Stars</b> The Brandon Sanderson Buddy Read and Epic Adventure continues with <a>Athena</a> and <a>Alexa</a>. I had so much fun reading this with these girls.<br><br>This is a fan’s book for sure. I loved every minute of it and all the references that wouldn’t have seemed important if you had not read the Mistborn trilogy first. It is 300 years since the rebirth and I have to say that some of my favorite things in the book are how the culture and religions of this time evolved around the characters that I loved from the original series; From Harmony’s forearms replacing Lord Ruler as a curse to the religions surrounding the Ascendant Warrior and The Survivor as well as the genealogy back to Lord Mistborn and the naming of cities streets and buildings.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/elendelashx_zpsae4b0fe9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402939599i/10015952._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo elendelashx_zpsae4b0fe9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>If that wasn’t enough for me to be happy Sanderson made sure that I had an entertaining and exciting story filled with mystery and great characters. This is a lighter book than the original Mistborn series and I enjoyed laughing with Wax, Marasi and Wayne.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/Waxashx_zps0118ee75.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402939599i/10015953._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Waxashx_zps0118ee75.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Waxillium has been out in the roughs acting as a lawman for years but is called back to Elendel after tragedy strikes and he is the only heir to his uncle’s house. He isn’t taking to the Lords life well and still itches to be a part of the action. Added to that is he needs to find someone to marry but his rough and tumble past is making that difficult. He does have one prospect but she is a little on the dry side compared to his sneakily snarky one.<br><br><i>“Lord Ladrian,” Steris said as they began eating, “I suggest that we begin compiling a list of conversational topics we can employ when in the company of others. The topics should not touch on politics or religion yet should be memorable and give us opportunities to appear charming. Do you know any particularly witty sayings or stories that can be our starting point?”<br>“I once shot the tail off a dog by mistake,” Waxillium said idly. “It’s kind of a funny story.”<br> “Shooting dogs is hardly appropriate dinner conversation,” Steris said.<br> “I know. Particularly since I was aiming for its balls.”</i><br><br>When railcars full of aluminum start to be stolen directly off the tracks vanishing into the Mists Wax is intrigued and egged on by Wayne a long-time friend from the roughs to join in the investigation. I freaking loved Wayne!!! <b>You want a book with a great bromance this is it</b>. The friendship that he and Wax has is phenomenal and hilarious.<br><br><b>
  <i>“You wanna know why I really came to find you?” Wayne asked.<br>“Why?”<br>“ I thought of you happy in a comfy bed, resting and relaxing, spending the rest of your life sipping tea and reading papers while people bring you food and maids rub your toes and stuff.”<br>“And?”<br>“ And I just couldn't leave you to a fate like that...I'm too good a friend to let a mate of mine die in such a terrible situation.”<br>“Comfortable?”<br>“No. Boring.”</i>
</b><br><br>They have known each other for so long and I totally ate up the dialogue between them and the quirkiness that was Wayne. He has an interesting way of looking at the world and he was never boring. <b>Sanderson easily creates some of the best side characters I’ve ever read.</b> Wayne steals the show, he is a hoot and a half and his philosophies on life just crack me up.<br><br><b>
  <i>“So,” Marasi said, “you traded a dead man’s scarf for another dead man’s gun. But…the gun itself belonged to someone dead, so by the same logic—”<br>“Don’t try,” Waxillium said. “Logic doesn’t work on Wayne.”<br>“I bought a ward against it off a traveling fortune-teller,” Wayne explained. “It lets me add two ’n’ two and get a pickle.”</i>
</b><br><br>AND NOW ONTO MY FAVORITE CHARACTER – I like Wayne but I’m team Marasi she is my girl!!! I know that Steris is the potential marriage partner for Wax but I love Marasi so I ship them together so hard. She and I are having a <b>hoemance</b> <i>that is the female equivalent of a bromance isn’t it?</i> She is like Hermione Granger all grown up meets Nancy Drew in my mind and I love it. Marasi was so full life and questions and so excited to get in on the action even though she is a little terrified of all of the things going on around her. She has a little hero worship going on for Wax as she has read all about his exploits in the roughs but even as she is getting to know the man Wax really is she takes it all in with this wonder and excitement that I love adored. Plus she seems to be able to hold her own with the boys too.<br><br><b>
  <i>He’s fine,” Wayne said, holding the door open for them. “I got quite near my entire rusted back blown off earlier, if you’ll kindly recall, and I didn’t hear nearly an ounce of the sympathy you’re showin’ him”<br>“That’s different,” Marasi said, walking part him.<br>“What? Why? ‘Cuz I can heal?”<br>“No,” she said, “because – even after knowing you only a short time – I’m fairly certain that on one level or another, you deserve to get blown up every now and again.”</i>
</b><br><br>I cross my fingers and hope that there is more in store in the future for Waxillium and Marasi, I think they could make a formidable couple solving crimes together.<br><br><b>The Story</b> - I don’t think Sanderson is capable of writing a bad story at this points. There were clues along the way to let you try and figure it out on your own but the mystery is still so good that I didn’t guess most of it. Plus there is still the wonderful immersement into different combinations of magic and mysticism. I’m always amazed with the sheer amount of information that can be packed into one of these novels and not in a tell you kind of way. Sanderson always shows you how things work and it is always entertaining in the process. <br><br>I can’t wait to read more of these characters. I almost loved this more than the original Mistborn series but I wouldn’t have loved it nearly as much if I didn’t have that foundation already. Such a great addition to the Mistborn world.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9310615177112258609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1607454991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1607454991" />
    <a title="Nafeeza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22200230-nafeeza"><img alt="Nafeeza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460654885p2/22200230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1607454991?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafeeza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafeeza" href="/user/show/22200230-nafeeza">Nafeeza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=fun-and-addictive">fun-and-addictive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=kick-ass-female-protagonist">kick-ass-female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=best-bromance">best-bromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22200230-nafeeza?shelf=awesome-characters">awesome-characters</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1607454991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10295131579689258297"><b>Review is up!</b><br/><br/>I admit one of the reasons I delayed reading this was because it was liken to the Western period and I am not a fan of that genre (don't read it, don't watch it), but I should have know that if anyone could make me like it, it would be Sanderson. This book takes place 300 hundred years after the original Mistborn Trilogy and is more light-hearted than its predecessor. That is not to say that the story is not of the same quality, quite the contrary. Wax returns home after 20 years in</span>
  <span id="freeText10295131579689258297" style="display:none"><b>Review is up!</b><br /><br />I admit one of the reasons I delayed reading this was because it was liken to the Western period and I am not a fan of that genre (don't read it, don't watch it), but I should have know that if anyone could make me like it, it would be Sanderson. This book takes place 300 hundred years after the original Mistborn Trilogy and is more light-hearted than its predecessor. That is not to say that the story is not of the same quality, quite the contrary. Wax returns home after 20 years in the Roughs due to the death of family members to become Lord of the House and assume the responsibilities that come with it. After a slew of crimes, he soon discovers that high society is more cunning and dangerous than the anything experienced in Roughs.<br /><br />Sanderson speciality is in crafting a world and characters so complex and transfixing that you forget everything else around you just to experience it for yourself and by the end you are sitting there with a smile on your face <i>(or more likely tears running down your cheeks)</i>, so thoroughly satisfied that you long to go back and read it again. <br /><br />So let's talk about the characters shall we; meet Waxillium Ladrian, Aka Wax - High Lord, "Sheriff" and Badass Extraordinaire. He is Twinborn (Coinshot and a Skimmer plus gun slinger), he is also funny to boot! Has mind for strategy and solving crimes. Then there is Wayne, the quick wit Deputy, master of disguises and "Trading". Collector of accents and hats and you do not want to end up on the business end of his dueling canes. His past is heart breaking but I love him even more for it. He is also a Twinshot (Bloodmaker and A Slider), his powers are very cool and interesting.<br /><br /><i>“You like the new duster?”<br />“Is that what took you so long? Please tell me you didn’t go shopping while I was fighting for my life.”<br />“Had to take out three gits that was guarding the entrance up above,” Wayne said, spinning his dueling canes. “One of them had this fine garment upon his person.” He hesitated. “I’m a little late ’cause I was trying to figure a way to beat him up without ruining the coat.”</i><br /><br />The bromance between these two were off the charts, I love their banter and how well they played off of each other. When they team up to fight, it is awesomeness to behold. They may just end up being my favorite pair EVER!<br /><br /><i>“Five left?” Waxillium asked.<br />“Six,” Wayne said, picking up and spinning his dueling canes. “There’s another in the shadows over there. I brought down seven. You?”<br />“Sixteen, I think,” Wax said distractedly. “Haven’t been counting carefully.”<br />“Sixteen? Damn, Wax. I was hoping you’d “have rusted a bit, was thinkin’ maybe I’d be able to catch you this time.”<br />Waxillium smiled. "It’s not a competition.” He hesitated. “Even if I am winning. Some men got out the door with Steris. I shot the guy who took your hat, though he lived. He’s probably gone by now.”<br />“You didn’t grab the hat for me?” Wayne asked, sounding offended.<br />“I was a little busy being shot at.”<br />“Busy? Aw, mate. It doesn’t take any effort at all to get shot at. I think you’re just makin’ excuses on account of being jealous of my lucky hat.”</i><br /><br />That is not to say that the ladies don't shine too. There is Marasi - a law student who is adorably strong willed and competent and Steris, man Steris is just so calculating and um... organized. <br /><i>“Waxillium shook his head, closing the contract. “Doesn’t this seem a little … stiff to you?”<br />“Stiff?”<br />“I mean, shouldn’t there be room for romance?”<br />“There is,” Steris said. “Page thirteen. Upon marriage, there shall be no more than three conjugal encounters per week and no fewer than one until a suitable heir is provided. After that, the same numbers apply to a two-week span.”</i><br /><br />*Snickers* See, organized, but she has depth and I look forward to exploring that further. A special shout out to Ranette, I met her briefly but it was love at first sight! I am so looking forward to these ladies development in the future. Sanderson did a great job expanding this world, making it seem new and exciting while still keeping parts that are reminiscent of the first era. I also enjoyed getting to dive even further into the the art of Allomancy and Feruchemy. And the little throw backs to the original cast made my heart sing. I was eating those little tidbits up faster than you can say <i>Harmony</i>. <br /><br />PS: I need to get my hands on Arcanum Unbounded right now!<br /><br />Thanks for the BR my lovelies <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10295131579689258297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_710520872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/710520872" />
    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/710520872?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer710520872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14778019474636111805">I remember having liked this book the first time around, but that it did disappoint me slightly. I wasn’t sure why, but having now reread it, I can say that it is better than I remembered and another excellent entry into the Mistborn series of trilogies.<br/> <br/>The problem I experienced the first time around, was that I was expecting another The Final Empire. That book blew me away the first time I read it. I had never read anything so imaginative or epic up to that point and it set the standard for me</span>
  <span id="freeText14778019474636111805" style="display:none">I remember having liked this book the first time around, but that it did disappoint me slightly. I wasn’t sure why, but having now reread it, I can say that it is better than I remembered and another excellent entry into the Mistborn series of trilogies.<br /> <br />The problem I experienced the first time around, was that I was expecting another The Final Empire. That book blew me away the first time I read it. I had never read anything so imaginative or epic up to that point and it set the standard for me by which I was to measure future forays into the world of fantasy books.<br /> <br />The second problem was that I fell in love with the characters in the first series and found it hard to part with them. There are a lot of references in this book to those characters, and although these reminders are cool, they also stirred a sense of sadness in me. I won’t get to see most of them again. I even feel sad that the characters from the different trilogies won’t get to meet each other and I guess that means that I need to tip my hat to Mr Sanderson and blame him for making me like the first trilogy too much.<br /><br />So to set this straight. <br /><br />This book is NOT a more modern version of the Final Empire, but it is a story set 300 years after the events in The Hero of Ages, and thus in a more modern world. It did not have that epic feel, but instead it was a light and fun story set in the same world with some pretty cool characters who kicked ass. Think allomancers in a steampunk western. Yep, mistborn style action in a world with guns and gadgets. These allomancers don’t have the powers of old, in fact nowadays they only ever possess one of the allomantic abilities. Some others have inherited a single feruchemical ability. And in rare cases there are twinborn with both. Meet Waxillium Ladrian AKA Wax.<br /><br />Wax is a lawman. He policed the Rough for many years, but has now returned to the city of Elendel and is being forced to change his gun-toting ways to fit in with civilized society. Events conspire however, that force his hand. Evil is afoot. Picking up his gun, cloak and hat again, he teams up with his old partner Wayne (who is weird, inappropriate and hilarious at the same time) and sets of to kick ass and solve mysteries. There is great banter between these two and Lady Marasi (a fact-quoting criminologist) who gets involved in helping them track the villains and solve the case. She also happens to bring a little romantic interest to the table that I hope we will see more of later on.<br /> <br />There is no question about it. This is a great book with awesome storytelling that deserves nothing less than five stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14778019474636111805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2236264712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2236264712" />
    <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword"><img alt="Iryna *Book and Sword*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547595130p2/57236678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2236264712?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105829" href="/book/show/10803710-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword?shelf=adult-fantasy">adult-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2236264712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6493311414782676483"><b>4.5/5 stars</b> (rounded up)<br/><br/><b>“It's all right Wayne," Waxillium said softly. "I've made a promise. I told Lord Harms I'd return Steris to him. And I will. That is that."<br/>"Then I will remain and help," Marasi said. "That is that."<br/>"And I could really use some food," Wayne added. "Fat is fat.”</b><br/><br/>​This quote right here is the most accurate description of the 3 main characters in <b>The Alloy of Law. </b><br/><br/>​Also, this book right here is the prime example of how to write a second generation series that doesn't suck, but</span>
  <span id="freeText6493311414782676483" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars</b> (rounded up)<br /><br /><b>“It's all right Wayne," Waxillium said softly. "I've made a promise. I told Lord Harms I'd return Steris to him. And I will. That is that."<br />"Then I will remain and help," Marasi said. "That is that."<br />"And I could really use some food," Wayne added. "Fat is fat.”</b><br /><br />​This quote right here is the most accurate description of the 3 main characters in <b>The Alloy of Law. </b><br /><br />​Also, this book right here is the prime example of how to write a second generation series that doesn't suck, but quite the opposite - shines almost as bright as the original. Did I miss the original cast: Elend, Vin, Breeze and the rest of them? Of course I did! I love them all to pieces. Did I wish for them to be in this book instead of the new characters? Heck NO! I loved the new ones right off the bat, and now I have more characters to add to my ever-growing bucket of ...well favorites. <br /><br /><b>“I need something, Wax. A place to look. You always did the thinking.”<br />“Yes, having a brain helps with that, surprisingly.”</b><br /><br />​<b>The Alloy of Law</b> is much shorter, and thus is not nearly as developed or interwoven as the first three books are - but that is the point. The next three books are meant to take the reader back to the same world (although hundreds of years later) but they also meant to make the reader laugh. And boy, they do! I don't remember a book that had me laughing so hard and so often! So what's funny you will ask? <br /><br /><b>“It’s what happens when you shoot someone,” Wayne pointed out. “At least, usually someone has the good sense to get dead when you go to all the trouble to shoot them.”</b><br /><br />The banter between Wax and Wayne is priceless. Priceless!! If you enjoyed the conversations between Breeze and Ham in the first trilogy, but wished for more, well - your wishes have been granted! Wax and Wayne are here to satisfy your thirst for witty banter. And they do so in tenfolds. <br /><br />I also enjoyed Maresi a lot and can't wait to see what direction her character development takes. Also, Steris? How can she be so dull, but hilariously entertaining at the same time?? Loved it! <br /><br /><b>The Alloy of Law</b> is short and to the point, but even if it looks like the plot has wrapped itself up - certain little things will ensure that the reader comes back for more. <br />Like, what was up with that ending??<br /><br /><b>“Once one becomes a man, he can and must make his own decisions. But I do offer warning. Even a good thing can become destructive if taken to excess.”</b><br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a><br />My <a href="https://bookandswordblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WORDPRESS BLOG</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6493311414782676483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2748117288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2748117288" />
    <a title="Bea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68155245-bea"><img alt="Bea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598741314p2/68155245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2748117288?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bea" href="/user/show/68155245-bea">Bea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575105836" href="/book/show/12065807-the-alloy-of-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68155245-bea?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68155245-bea?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68155245-bea?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68155245-bea?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68155245-bea?shelf=sanderson">sanderson</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2748117288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16454304357664897025"><b>Definitely my favourite in the series so far!</b> This was such an intense book I loved every minute of it. <br/><br/>Set 300 years after The Final Empire (books 1-3) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[and the fall of the Lord Ruler <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the series is about how the world is still adapting to the changes and how some groups are still trying to cause chaos.<br/><br/>The world building is phenomenal, it's nothing like your typical fantasy since it's set I guess if the industrial revolution started in the year 300? Different date,</span>
  <span id="freeText16454304357664897025" style="display:none"><b>Definitely my favourite in the series so far!</b> This was such an intense book I loved every minute of it. <br /><br />Set 300 years after The Final Empire (books 1-3) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and the fall of the Lord Ruler <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the series is about how the world is still adapting to the changes and how some groups are still trying to cause chaos.<br /><br />The world building is phenomenal, it's nothing like your typical fantasy since it's set I guess if the industrial revolution started in the year 300? Different date, same world. I was hooked by the writing as soon as I began reading, not expecting it to be as good as book 1 of the series but it was and I was blown away.<br /><br />This is only book 4 but I can already say I'm going to enjoy this series more than I did the original trilogy. While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68428.The_Final_Empire__Mistborn___1_" title="The Final Empire (Mistborn, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a> was mind-blowing, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68429.The_Well_of_Ascension__Mistborn___2_" title="The Well of Ascension (Mistborn, #2) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767793.The_Hero_of_Ages__Mistborn___3_" title="The Hero of Ages (Mistborn, #3) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages</a> sadly did not work well for me.<br /><br />The characters are honestly some of the best in a fantasy world I've read. Wayne (my absolute favourite) is just so funny! The humour is on point in the book and it contrasts really well with the dramatic fight scenes that pop up at times. Even when something is really serious he's being funny, I can't tell you the amount of times I laughed out loud at the book in public.<br /><br />Like, just read it.<br /><br /><i>While it's possible to read book 4 onward without the original trilogy, I didn't realise how many references there would be of that trilogy in this book and probably later on too. So I definitely recommend reading 1-3 first.</i><br /><br /><b>The Final Empire: 4.5 stars<br />The Well of Ascension: 3.5 stars<br />The Hero of Ages: 3 stars<br />The Alloy of Law: 5 stars!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16454304357664897025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_168545352" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168545352" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168545352?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=fangirl-alert">fangirl-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=favorite-2012-reads">favorite-2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=not-for-the-sensitive">not-for-the-sensitive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168545352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4548376296500392823">Fair warning: I am a massive Sanderson fangirl. This is a fair approximation of my behavior whenever I read one of his books:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703889.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I babble at people who have no idea what I'm talking about, I trip over my own feet and nearly down the stairs, I fling my arms around as if they are not attached to my body and can actually be thrown; I am loud and exuberant and wholly consumed by excitement and while I'm sure the extremely out-of-character nature of this behavior terrifies some people around me no end, I</span>
  <span id="freeText4548376296500392823" style="display:none">Fair warning: I am a massive Sanderson fangirl. This is a fair approximation of my behavior whenever I read one of his books:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703889.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I babble at people who have no idea what I'm talking about, I trip over my own feet and nearly down the stairs, I fling my arms around as if they are not attached to my body and can actually be thrown; I am loud and exuberant and wholly consumed by excitement and while I'm sure the extremely out-of-character nature of this behavior terrifies some people around me no end, I can't help but think of it as really quite an ideal state.<br>Thankfully I read most of this book alone (between the hours of 11pm and 1am the night before my noon flight back to college, in a frenetic attempt to finish the library copy I'd checked out which eventually ended in exhausted admission of defeat) or with another fangirl (who I introduced to the Mistborn trilogy this past semester and who is now most of the way finished with Hero of Ages). We spent hours sitting across from each other listening to movie soundtracks and occasionally speaking to quote funny bits of dialogue or to bemoan the choices made by favorite characters. It is an excellent way to pass the time on a Friday night and anyone who says otherwise can FIGHT ME.<br><br><br>Anyhow, the book. Riiiiight. The only honest evaluation of my response to it is really one long squee - from the maps to the Ars Arcanum I was just freaking out the whole time. It's hard to review (ye gods, aren't they all?) because a lot of my FEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEELINGS are tied up in callbacks to the original trilogy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(The Ascendant Warrior and the Last Emperor - I I I kind of almost cried when their <i>tombs</i> were mentioned, agh how can they be dead I AM STILL NOT OVER THE END OF HERO OF AGES GODDAMMIT. And the Lord Mistborn - I see what you did there - and Wax is descended from Breeze - and <i>Harmony</i> aaaaaaaaaaah best deity ever I love him so much I can't even-) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I can't pry off that lens even if I wanted to - and I don't because this just felt like a love letter to the characters I adore - and tell you what this book's empirical merits are, not really. I will try. I will probably fail, but I will try.<br><br>So first of all, there's Wax. Waxillium Ladrian, I suppose, but I like Wax better.<br>My thoughts on Wax:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703890.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Okay, yeah, but not really, I guess. I totally understand how Marasi was so taken with him, though - he's capable, witty, honest, loyal, noble, courageous, skilled, and I will bet you anything he cuts a fiiiiiine figure in a mistcoat. He also has some lovely internal conflict, courtesy of the tragic loss he suffers in the prologue, and I liked seeing the battle between fear and sense of duty raging in his head. Now, I'll be honest: there is a possibility that Wax is something of a Gary-Stu. Other characters describe him reverentially in a way that made me roll my eyes; most notably, as like "a one-of-a-kind painting, a masterpiece". But I really cannot be arsed to care about his possible Stuishness. The sheer fun of reading about a character like him, combined with the incredibly badass fight scenes (which I want to see on a screen so. badly.) really quite overwhelm any objections I could otherwise be inclined to raise.<br><br>And then there's Wayne, Wax's best friend and deputy in the Roughs.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703891.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He's no Wax, stealing my heart (Wayne would say 'trading for it', I suppose) but he's a pretty wonderful character in and of himself - his childish enthusiasm, his brilliant insight into people, his humor (albeit occasionally unintentional, as in the case of the 'broad education' pun which I think was my favorite), and most of all for his past and what he's done about it. Not to spoil anything, but he is a poor sweet darling and I just want to give him lots of hugs and tell him he's doing the right thing.<br><br>Finally, last but certainly not least, is Marasi.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703892.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I read something lately where someone was talking about the fact that the feminist movement asked Hollywood for 'strong female characters' and Hollywood gave them 'STRONG female characters' with lots of swords and general ass-kicking, when actually what they wanted was 'strong characters, female' depicted in the many varieties of imperfect strength that men are shown in. Well, here's one - a woman who is a dab hand with a rifle but would rather enjoy the comforts of a city and pursue justice through legal work than go out and be a hero; a young woman, with the kind of vulnerable sad crush that young women get on someone they admire, who nonetheless gets shit done before she worries about romance. She's awesome and I really, really, really enjoyed her.<br><br><br>On a broader note, the worldbuilding. There is, I am sad to say, insufficient Vin worship for my tastes. If you ask me, that woman should be the grand high goddess of Scadrial - yes, the entire planet, even the people on the other side of the world who haven't heard of her - forever and ever. Buuut they didn't ask me, so I have to be content with a town, a month, and a really epic gun named after her. (The gun is called 'Vindication' and is super awesome.)<br>Instead of omnipresent Vin worship, there are three main religions - Survivorism, Pathism, and Splinterism. If you've read the first three books, identifying their major figures should be a piece of cake; if not, just enjoy them as backdrop. Unlike a lot of Sanderson's books, religion does not actually play a huge role here; it's more casually nodded to than anything else.<br>Scadrial's advancements in 300 years are really fun, though there are some things I find disappointing. Due to dilution of the gene pool, there are no more Mistborn, which is tragic; there are, however, Twinborn instead - people with both allomantic and feruchemical powers. And there are a lot of new metals with cool new uses. (Temporal metals. TEMPORAL METALS.) Technology has also changed and while this book is not quiiiiite as steampunk as its cover makes it look, it is still loads of fun to see all of this marvelous magic interacting with growing skyscrapers and trains.<br><br><br>Aaaand that's really all I feel about saying about that. Wild blatherings and possible theorizing below in the spoilers; tread with care.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Before he dies, Miles says "One day, the men of gold and red, bearers of the final metal, <i>will</i> come to you. And you <i>will</i> be ruled by them." I am really inclined to plant a flag in this and declare it OBVIOUS COSMERE STUFF but maybe I'm wrong? Maybe it has to do with the people on the other side of the planet, whose existence Sanderson has previously confirmed - though I think he also said that they didn't have any of the Metallic Arts so maybe not. The mention of red kind of makes me wonder if they're the Voidbrngers from The Way of Kings, but their color scheme was red and black, wasn't it? And what is this 'final metal' business? Could it be another God Metal, like atium and larasium, made presumably by another Shard? Could it, in fact, be the substance that the shards are shards OF?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349941ra/703893.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I kind of want the bad guys to get away with their breeding program so that maybe there will be Mistborn in the next trilogy. I am well aware of how horrible I am for wanting this. It does not change the fact that I will be very sad to read another Mistborn book without any actual Mistborn.<br><br>Marsh describes Wax as "doing my brother's work" near the end - which makes me wonder how much Kel can communicate with Sazed and thus Marsh. I think there are dimensions or planes involved or something like that and they confuse me. I like the idea of Kelsier and Sazed being co-gods, though. That would be neat.<br><br>The mention of Hemalurgy being the art of greatest interest to the Cosmere has me really really worried.<br><br>ALLOYS OF THE GOD METALS. Sixteen new alloys per metal. Oh my goodness. I want to see it, I really really do.<br><br>Some of the Ferring abilities - storing determination or storing Investiture itself - simply incredible. I cannot wait to see this all explored more.<br><br>What is a Spiritweb? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In conclusion: SANDERSON WRITE MORE BOOKS MORE FASTER.<br>please.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4548376296500392823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KLfkjkd1alXo5ILbim2R00S2IcDJ5q2ik2DDfXwIWOT8Ir9HxOTvDm8vlss6XcHAHzOxQFiQWk70cQ9/VBKoEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IkraydMJFhVugEWpxJnl0UF78A5yKr+UQZDAAin8ZOT234EAUJiTTulLUbl0qbXCGv5gjuNcSHgmgQwAAeaUEA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12784235890597359435">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText12784235890597359435" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12784235890597359435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
